# Internal Openness: From Natural Numbers to the Ontology of Physical Reality

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXII, XLIV, VII, XXXIII

---

## Abstract

This paper proposes a unifying ontological thesis: the world is not best understood as a system embedded in a fixed background of possibilities (a closed state space with an "outside"), but as a generative structure that is **internally open**. Internal openness means that the admissible space of possibilities is not a static set but a generator: it can expand by the world's own dynamics, without requiring an external reservoir of states. We argue that the clearest mathematical prototype of internal openness is the generative ontology of the natural numbers $\mathbb{N}$, understood not as a completed totality but as a process whose continuation is locally well-defined while globally unbounded. The same ontological pattern illuminates foundational puzzles in physics, including the origin of the thermodynamic arrow of time and the status of entropy in the presence of evolving admissibility domains. We also show how classical distinctions such as "open vs. closed systems" in thermodynamics inherit a Newtonian absolutism and become secondary when internal openness is adopted as the primitive notion.

**Keywords:** internal openness, generative ontology, natural numbers, arrow of time, entropy, admissibility domain

---

## 1. Introduction

Physics and mathematics are often presented as distinct enterprises: mathematics supplies formal language; physics supplies empirical content. Yet some mathematical structures appear to encode constraints so basic that they function less like descriptive tools and more like **ontological signatures** of what a world can be.

This paper advances a single organizing idea: **internal openness**.

The dominant classical picture, inherited from Newtonian mechanics, assumes a **fixed arena** of all possibilities. In thermodynamics this appears as the open/closed distinction: a system is "open" if it exchanges matter or energy with an "outside," and "closed" if it does not. In statistical mechanics it appears as a fixed phase space or a fixed energy shell. In many foundational debates it appears as an implicit premise that **all possibilities exist "at once,"** and dynamics merely permutes them.

We propose that this picture is **not ontologically necessary**. A system may be open *internally*: it may generate new admissible possibilities without being open to something outside. Once this shift is made, several classical paradoxes lose their force (not by modifying mathematics, but by revising the ontological background on which the mathematics is applied).

Our main claim is that internal openness has a clean mathematical prototype: **the natural numbers, understood generatively**. Studying $\mathbb{N}$ in this way becomes, quite literally, a study of the world's most basic physics—not by numerological symbolism, but by identifying structural constraints that any non-artifactual reality must satisfy.

---

## 2. Background Absolutism and the Open/Closed Inheritance

The Newtonian worldview suggests an ontological template:

1. a fixed state space $X$ (space, phase space, configuration space),
2. a dynamics acting on $X$,
3. systems as subsets of $X$ whose openness is defined by boundary exchange with $X \setminus \text{system}$.

Within this template, **"openness" is necessarily relational**: it presupposes an exterior domain into which the system can couple.

> **Thesis 1 (Secondary status of boundary openness).** The classical open/closed distinction is *secondary*: it presupposes a fixed background of possibilities. If the admissible domain of possibilities can evolve, then the primary question is not boundary exchange but the ontological evolution of admissibility itself.

The point is not that boundary exchange is unimportant in practice. Rather, it is **not the deepest concept**. The deepest concept is whether a world is a completed artifact—a closed list of possibilities—or a generative reality whose admissible space is itself dynamic.

---

## 3. Internal Openness: A Minimal Definition

We define internal openness at the level of possibility spaces.

> **Definition 1 (Admissibility domain).** Let $\Omega$ denote a reference space of conceivable descriptions. An *admissibility domain* is a subset $\Gamma(t) \subseteq \Omega$ representing the states regarded as physically admissible at time $t$, given the world's constraints.

> **Definition 2 (Internal openness).** A world is *internally open* if $\Gamma(t)$ is not fixed once and for all. In particular, there exist times $t_1 < t_2$ such that $\Gamma(t_1) \subsetneq \Gamma(t_2)$, or more generally the structure of admissibility evolves (including changes of dimension, effective degrees of freedom, or constraints).

> **Remark 1.** Internal openness is **not** the same as coupling to an exterior reservoir. It is a statement about the ontology of the admissible domain: admissibility is *generated* and can expand "from within."

This definition is deliberately minimal. It does not prejudge the physics (classical, quantum, cosmological). It only asserts that treating the space of possibilities as a static, completed set is an **optional assumption**, not a necessity.

---

## 4. Natural Numbers as a Prototype of Internal Openness

The natural numbers are usually introduced as a completed set obeying axioms (e.g., Peano). A generative ontology shifts emphasis: $\mathbb{N}$ is not primarily a completed totality but a **rule of continuation**.

### 4.1 Completion vs. Generation

A completed-set view invites a background absolutism: all numbers exist "already," and we merely access them. A generative view instead highlights the asymmetry between:

| Aspect | Description |
|:-------|:------------|
| **Local determinacy** | From any given stage, the continuation rule is well-defined |
| **Global non-closure** | There is no final stage, no last element, no completed container of all possibilities |

> **Thesis 2 (Arithmetic openness).** The most primitive expression of internal openness is: **continuation without closure**. $\mathbb{N}$ provides a minimal formal model of this property.

This is already an ontological statement: a reality compatible with internal openness must allow "more" without requiring an external supplement. It must allow novelty without an external designer.

### 4.2 Atoms and Local Necessity

In a generative reading, **"atomic" elements** are those that become necessary to maintain generativity and completeness under the allowed operations. In standard arithmetic, primes exemplify a robust form of irreducible novelty: they cannot be decomposed within a chosen multiplicative structure. In a generative ontology, their appearance is interpretable as a **local necessity** rather than a globally precomputed placement.

This motivates a distinctive philosophical criterion:

> **Thesis 3 (No transcendental control criterion).** If a generative structure requires global foreknowledge to maintain local completeness, it ceases to be genuinely generative and becomes artifact-like. A "counterexample" to natural generativity would require a form of *transcendental control* over future constraints.

Here "transcendental" means external to the internal generative rules, not mystical. The point is structural: internal openness forbids global steering that anticipates future states to enforce present constraints.

### 4.3 Extensions of Number Systems as Ontological Expansions

One of the strongest signals of internal openness in $\mathbb{N}$ is that it naturally enables further structures:

$$\mathbb{N} \to \mathbb{Z} \to \mathbb{Q} \to \mathbb{R} \to \mathbb{C} \to \mathbb{H} \text{ (quaternions)} \to \cdots$$

These extensions are **not arbitrary inventions**. Each extension resolves a structurally generated limitation:

| Extension | Resolves |
|:----------|:---------|
| $\mathbb{Z}$ | absence of subtraction closure |
| $\mathbb{Q}$ | absence of division closure |
| $\mathbb{R}$ | completion under limits |
| $\mathbb{C}$ | closure for algebraic problems (e.g., roots of polynomials) |
| $\mathbb{H}$ | deeper demand: faithful representation of rotations and orientation |

> **Remark 2.** The "escape forward" mechanism is **generative**: problems produced by the current ontology force an expansion of admissible entities. This is internal openness expressed in pure form.

This is the precise sense in which **number theory becomes "fundamental physics"**: it studies the minimal conditions under which a world can sustain continuation, closure demands, and irreducible novelty without external steering.

---

## 5. From Arithmetic to Physics: Evolving Admissibility and the Arrow of Time

Internal openness becomes physically potent when applied to entropy and time. Classical paradoxes of reversibility and recurrence are typically derived under a **fixed arena assumption**: a measure-preserving dynamics on a fixed, finite-measure domain.

### 5.1 Two Levels of Entropy

Internal openness naturally distinguishes:

| Level | Measure |
|:------|:--------|
| **State entropy** | Relative to a chosen coarse-graining |
| **Admissibility entropy** | A measure of the size of the admissible domain |

Let $\mathbb{P}$ be a reference measure on $(\Omega, \mathcal{F})$ in the Kolmogorov sense. Define:

$$S_{\Gamma}(t) \coloneqq \log \mathbb{P}(\Gamma(t))$$

If $\Gamma(t)$ expands in measure, $S_{\Gamma}(t)$ is **non-decreasing**. This is not the thermodynamic entropy of a subsystem; it is an ontological measure of increasing admissibility.

Meanwhile, for a partition $\mathcal{P}_t$ (or equivalently a $\sigma$-algebra encoding distinguishability), define a local Shannon entropy:

$$H_{\mathcal{P}_t}(t) \coloneqq -\sum_{C \in \mathcal{P}_t} \mathbb{P}(C \mid \Gamma(t)) \log \mathbb{P}(C \mid \Gamma(t))$$

Local order can increase (local entropy decreases) while $S_{\Gamma}(t)$ increases, because they are defined at different levels.

### 5.2 Why the Classical Paradoxes Lose Force

Recurrence arguments require a **fixed, finite-measure space** invariant under the dynamics. If $\Gamma(t)$ evolves, the relevant invariance conditions fail at the ontological level: there is no single fixed domain on which recurrence can be asserted globally.

Similarly, the Loschmidt reversal assumes that time-reversal maps admissible states to admissible states in the same arena. Internal openness allows that **time-reversal symmetry of microscopic equations is compatible with ontological asymmetry of admissibility**.

> **Thesis 4 (Arrow of time from internal openness).** The thermodynamic arrow of time can be understood as a manifestation of increasing admissibility: the growth of $\Gamma(t)$ (and the evolution of relevant coarse-grainings) makes global time-reversal and recurrence arguments inapplicable as universal objections.

This is conceptually parallel to arithmetic: the continuation rule is locally well-defined, but the totality is not given. The arrow of time is, in this view, **not an extra postulate glued onto reversible laws**, but an intrinsic feature of a generative world.

---

## 6. Coarse-Graining as Evolving $\sigma$-Algebras (Kolmogorov Clarity)

A frequent confusion in entropy debates is the tacit treatment of probability as absolute. Kolmogorov's framework makes explicit that probabilities are defined on a **chosen $\sigma$-algebra**: what counts as an event depends on what distinctions are meaningful.

Coarse-graining corresponds to passing to a **coarser $\sigma$-algebra**. In an internally open world, the relevant $\sigma$-algebra can **evolve**: new stable structures make new distinctions causally real and measurable. This is not epistemic arbitrariness; it is the **objective emergence** of stable macroscopic categories.

The arithmetic analogy is direct: new number systems emerge when old ones cannot express required operations. Likewise, new macroscopic observables become relevant when the world generates new stable structures.

---

## 7. Objections and Clarifications

### 7.1 Is This Merely Semantic?

**No.** The framework does not redefine words; it changes which assumptions are primitive. Fixed-arena models are not declared false; they are treated as effective approximations within regimes where $\Gamma(t)$ is effectively stable.

### 7.2 Does Internal Openness Deny Conservation Laws?

**No.** Local conservation laws can hold within a given admissibility regime. Internal openness concerns whether the space of admissible regimes itself is fixed. The existence of effective degrees of freedom and phase transitions already suggests that the ontology of admissibility is layered.

### 7.3 Is This Numerology?

**No.** Numerology assigns mystical meanings to particular numbers. This paper uses the natural numbers as a **structural prototype of generativity**: continuation without closure, local necessity of novelty, and forced expansions of ontology. These are formal constraints, not symbolic associations.

---

## 8. Conclusion

We proposed **internal openness** as a primitive ontological notion: a world may be open not by exchange with an external domain, but by **internal generation of admissible possibilities**. The natural numbers, read generatively, provide a minimal and exceptionally clear model of this ontology: local determinacy combined with global non-closure, and the forced expansion into richer structures when limitations arise.

When the same template is applied to physics, foundational puzzles around entropy and the arrow of time become less mysterious. Classical objections rely on a fixed background arena of possibilities. Internal openness removes that hidden absolutism: **the arena itself is part of the world and can evolve**.

In this sense, the study of $\mathbb{N}$ is not a poetic metaphor for physics. It is a study of the **minimal generative constraints that any non-artifactual reality must satisfy**.

---

## 9. Connection to Codex Rerum

This article is foundational for multiple Codex modules:

| Module | Connection |
|:-------|:-----------|
| **Module XXXII: Thermodynamics of Open Possibility** | Internal openness is the ontological basis for $d\Omega/dt > 0$ |
| **Module XLIV: Additive Physics** | $\mathbb{N}$ as generative prototype for AFN |
| **Module VII: Cosmological Unification** | The evolution of $\Gamma(t)$ as the universe's admissibility domain |
| **Module XXXIII: Sovereignty and Identity** | Internal openness as the foundation for genuine autonomy |

[2] K. Młynarski, "Generative Ontology of Natural Numbers: Additive Atomhood, Continuity of Generation, and Goldbach Properties," Preprint on ResearchGate, 2026.

# Goldbach's Conjecture in Sieve-Generated Arithmetic
## A Proof via Conservation of Algorithmic Work within LocalSieveAlg

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate, January 2026  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXIV, XXXVI, XLIV, XLV, XLVI

---

## Abstract

We formalize the Goldbach Conjecture as a theorem within the arithmetic structure $\mathfrak{N}_{S} \coloneqq (\mathbb{N}, +, \times, D_{S})$, generated by a deterministic, local Binary Sieve. This work operates strictly within a generative model governed by Algorithmic Work constraints and does not claim to be a proof in Peano Arithmetic. We define a class of algorithms LocalSieveAlg and a canonical cost model based on layer probes. We prove that a "Resonant State" (a counterexample to Goldbach) would create a structural "Oracle of Compositeness," allowing for a significant algorithmic speedup that violates the Axiom of Computational Irreducibility. Thus, Goldbach's conjecture is established as a necessary theorem within the model $\mathfrak{N}_{S}$.

**Keywords:** Goldbach conjecture, binary sieve, algorithmic work, computational irreducibility, sieve-generated arithmetic

---

## 1. Introduction

In the Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN), the generation of prime numbers is viewed as a process that converts computational work into structural information. We postulate that this work follows a conservation law: **there are no "free" bits of information about primality**.

We define a formal universe $\mathfrak{N}_{S}$ where the generation of atoms (primes) is governed by a strict cost model. We demonstrate that the existence of a Goldbach-Resonant state would imply a "free lunch": a method to determine the compositeness of a significant fraction of numbers without performing the requisite layer probes.

> **Key Insight:** The Goldbach conjecture is not an isolated arithmetic fact but a consequence of the conservation of algorithmic work in the sieve-generated structure.

---

## 2. The Sieve-Generated Structure

> **Definition 2.1 (Sieve-Generated Structure).** Let $\mathcal{S}$ be a deterministic Binary Sieve (as described in [1]). The structure is defined as:
> $$\mathfrak{N}_{S} \coloneqq (\mathbb{N}, +, \times, D_{S})$$
> where $D_{S}(n) = 1$ if $n$ is an atom (prime) and $0$ otherwise.

### 2.1 Canonical Cost Model

To define "speedup" rigorously, we define the unit of work in terms of the sieve's internal operations.

> **Definition 2.2 (Layer-Probe Cost).** Let $\tau(n)$ denote the number of "layer probes" performed by the sieve to determine $D_{S}(n)$.
> - A **probe** consists of checking the condition $n \equiv 0 \pmod{p}$ against an active layer $p$.
> - To identify $n$ as composite ($D(n) = 0$), the sieve stops at the first successful probe.
> - To identify $n$ as an atom ($D(n) = 1$), the sieve must probe against all active layers (up to the cutoff $\sqrt{n}$).

We postulate two structural conditions regarding the distribution of this cost:

> **Condition 2.1 (Atom Maximal Cost).** If $D_{\mathcal{S}}(n) = 1$, then $\tau(n) \geq \pi(\sqrt{n})$. Verifying an atom requires maximal work.

> **Condition 2.2 (Composite Typical Cost).** There exists a non-decreasing function $g(N)$ such that for any interval $(N/2, N]$, the cost $\tau(n) \geq g(N)$ for a fraction $\alpha > 0$ of the numbers.

**Justification:** While some composites are divisible by small primes (low cost), a constant density of numbers have smallest prime factors that grow with $N$, requiring multiple probes.

> **Definition 2.3 (Cumulative Work).** The total work of a generator $\mathcal{A}$ is:
> $$\mathcal{W}_{\mathcal{A}}(N) = \sum_{n=2}^{N} \tau_{\mathcal{A}}(n)$$

---

## 3. The Class LocalSieveAlg and Irreducibility

We restrict our analysis to algorithms that respect the generative constraints of the model.

> **Definition 3.1 (Class LocalSieveAlg).** An algorithm $\mathcal{A}$ belongs to **LocalSieveAlg** if:
> 1. It outputs $D(2), D(3), \ldots, D(N)$ in strictly increasing order.
> 2. It may maintain auxiliary marked sets or arrays derived only from the already computed history $D[1 \ldots n-1]$.
> 3. At stage $n$, it determines $D(n)$ using history, the target $N$, and local layer probes.
> 4. It has no access to external precomputed tables or non-sieve oracles.

> **Axiom 3.1 (G2: Irreducibility within LocalSieveAlg).** The standard sieve $\mathcal{S}$ is optimal within its class. There exists no algorithm $\mathcal{A} \in \text{LocalSieveAlg}$ such that:
> $$\mathcal{W}_{\mathcal{A}}(N) \leq (1 - \epsilon) \mathcal{W}_{\mathcal{S}}(N) \quad \text{for sufficiently large } N, \text{ with } \epsilon > 0.$$

> **Lemma 3.1 (Upper-Half Work Lower Bound).** Assume the Composite Typical Cost condition. Then for large $N$, the work in the upper half satisfies:
> $$\sum_{n = N/2 + 1}^{N} \tau(n) \geq \alpha \cdot \frac{N}{2} \cdot g(N)$$

*Proof.* By Condition 2.2, at least $\alpha (N/2)$ numbers in the interval have cost $\geq g(N)$. The sum follows directly. $\square$

---

## 4. The Algorithmic Speedup Theorem

> **Definition 4.1 (Resonant State).** For an even $N$, a **Resonant State** is defined by $C_N = 0$, implying:
> $$\forall p \in [2, N-2]:\quad D_{S}(p) = 1 \Rightarrow D_{S}(N - p) = 0$$

> **Lemma 4.1 (The Oracle of Compositeness).** Conditional on the Resonant State assumption, knowing that $p$ is an atom ($p < N/2$) provides a deterministic certificate that $N - p$ is composite.

> **Theorem 4.1 (Algorithmic Speedup).** If a Resonant State exists for $N$, there exists an algorithm $\mathcal{A}_{\text{res}} \in \text{LocalSieveAlg}$ that violates Axiom G2.

*Construction and Proof.*

**Phase 1:** Run the standard sieve for $n \in [1, N/2]$. Output $D(n)$ sequentially.

**Phase 2 (Auxiliary Marking):** Initialize an auxiliary array $M[N/2 + 1 \ldots N]$ to "Unknown". Whenever an atom $p$ is found in Phase 1, mark $M[N - p] \leftarrow$ "Composite".

*Locality Check:* This uses only $p$ (history) and $N$ (input). It does not access $D(k)$ for any $k > n$.

**Phase 3:** For $n \in [N/2 + 1, N]$:
- Check $M[n]$. If $M[n] =$ "Composite", output $D(n) = 0$ (Cost: $O(1)$).
- Else, run standard sieve probes $\tau(n)$ and output result.

**Work Analysis:** Let $S_{\text{skip}} = \{N - p : p \in \mathbb{P}, p \leq N/2\}$. The size is $|S_{\text{skip}}| = \pi(N/2) = \Theta(N / \log N)$.

The standard sieve performs work $\sum_{m \in S_{\text{skip}}} \tau(m)$ on these numbers. $\mathcal{A}_{\text{res}}$ performs work $\sum_{m \in S_{\text{skip}}} O(1)$.

The saved work is:
$$\Delta W \approx \sum_{m \in S_{\text{skip}}} (\tau(m) - O(1))$$

By the Composite Typical Cost condition, a significant fraction of $S_{\text{skip}}$ requires work $\geq g(N)$. Thus:
$$\Delta W = \Omega\left(\frac{N}{\log N} \cdot g(N)\right)$$

> **Remark 4.1.** The contradiction with Axiom G2 follows whenever the term $\Omega\left(\frac{N}{\log N} g(N)\right)$ dominates $\epsilon \mathcal{W}_{\mathcal{S}}(N)$ for sufficiently large $N$. Assuming the sieve's total work grows polynomially (e.g., $N \cdot \text{avg\_cost}$), and $g(N)$ is not negligible (e.g., related to $\log N$ or layer depth), the skip-induced saving constitutes a non-vanishing fraction of the canonical work.

---

## 5. The Structure Theorem

> **Theorem 5.1 (Goldbach Necessity in $\mathfrak{N}_{S}$).** In the model $\mathfrak{N}_{S}$ governed by Axioms G1 and G2, Goldbach's conjecture holds for sufficiently large $N$.

*Proof.* Assume $C_N = 0$. By the Algorithmic Speedup Theorem, there exists $\mathcal{A}_{\text{res}} \in \text{LocalSieveAlg}$ strictly more efficient than the irreducible sieve. This violates Axiom G2. Thus, $C_N > 0$. $\square$

---

## 6. Discussion: The Nature of the Proof

### 6.1 What This Proof Establishes

This proof establishes Goldbach's conjecture **within the sieve-generated structure $\mathfrak{N}_{S}$**, under the axioms:

- **Atom Maximal Cost:** Verifying primality requires maximal work
- **Composite Typical Cost:** A positive density of composites in any interval requires non-trivial work
- **Irreducibility (G2):** The standard sieve is optimal within LocalSieveAlg

### 6.2 Why This Is Not a Proof in Peano Arithmetic

The proof relies on **computational and cost-theoretic axioms** that are not derivable from Peano arithmetic alone. It assumes:

1. A specific generative model of numbers (the Binary Sieve)
2. A cost model for algorithmic work
3. An optimality axiom for the sieve

These are **meta-mathematical** assumptions about how numbers are generated, not purely arithmetic statements.

### 6.3 The Philosophical Significance

The proof shows that Goldbach's conjecture is **not an isolated accident** but a structural consequence of the way primes are generated. A counterexample would imply:

- An "Oracle of Compositeness" — a way to know compositeness without work
- A violation of the conservation of algorithmic work
- A breakdown of the generative model

> **A world with a false Goldbach conjecture would be a world where information about primality can be obtained "for free" — a world with algorithmic miracles.**

---

# Combinatorial Redundancy and Structural Goldbach: A Dual Approach via Additive Semigroups and Structural Entropy

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate, January 2026  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXIV, XXXVI, XLIV, XLVIII, XLIX

---

## Abstract

We present a constructive approach to the Goldbach Conjecture based on the theory of Restrictive Additive Semigroups within the framework of Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN). We distinguish between **Monogenic Addition** (linear extension, $p + p$) and **Polygenic Addition** (mixing, $p + q$). We demonstrate that prime numbers act as **"Gap-Fillers"** designed to maximize the coverage of the monogenic skeleton. We introduce the concept of **Structural Entropy** to quantify the distribution of generators across arithmetic progressions. We prove that a counterexample to Goldbach's conjecture implies a state of **"Anti-Symmetry"** with abnormally low structural entropy. Finally, we provide a unified roadmap (The Duality Dictionary), demonstrating that the "Resonant State" (in Sieve Theory) and the "Semigroup Void" (in Additive Theory) are dual manifestations of the same forbidden structural anomaly.

**Keywords:** Goldbach conjecture, additive semigroups, structural entropy, anti-symmetry, combinatorial redundancy, duality

---

## 1. Introduction

In the AFN framework, natural numbers are not static entities but the result of a dynamic evolution of additive semigroups. This paper explores the **"Combinatorial Redundancy"** that arises when a system optimized for linear coverage (primes filling gaps) begins to interact nonlinearly.

We formalize the intuition that **"the cloud of sums is too dense to leave a hole."** By defining Structural Entropy, we show that a missing Goldbach pair requires the primes to conspire in a way that violates their own generative imperative of quasi-uniform distribution.

> **Key Insight:** The Goldbach conjecture is a consequence of the tension between two types of addition: the linear extension of primes (monogenic) and their nonlinear mixing (polygenic). The quadratic surplus of polygenic sums makes holes impossible.

---

## 2. The Generative Framework

### 2.1 Monogenic vs. Polygenic Addition

> **Definition 2.1 (Monogenic Semigroup).** Let $A$ be a set of generators. The *monogenic semigroup* $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{mono}}(A)$ is the set of numbers formed by adding an element to itself:
> $$\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{mono}}(A) = \{n \cdot a \mid a \in A, n \in \mathbb{N}_{\geq 1}\}$$
> In visual terms, the monogenic semigroup represents a set of disjoint rays originating from the generators.

> **Definition 2.2 (Polygenic Semigroup).** The *polygenic semigroup* involves mixing distinct elements. We focus on the sumset:
> $$\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{poly}}^{(2)}(A) = A + A = \{a_i + a_j \mid a_i, a_j \in A\}$$

### 2.2 Primes as Gap-Fillers

> **Definition 2.3 (The $n = 1$ Principle).** A number $p$ is a *New Generator* (prime) if it cannot be covered by the Monogenic Semigroup of smaller generators:
> $$p \notin \mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{mono}}(\{a < p\})$$
> This implies that primes are introduced specifically to **break regularities** and **fill gaps** in the linear structure.

---

## 3. Combinatorial Redundancy

> **Lemma 3.1 (The Surplus Lemma).** Let $\pi(N) = |A \cap [1, N]|$.

> 1. The number of monogenic sums $(p + p)$ is $\pi(N)$.
> 2. The number of polygenic sums $(p + q$ with $p \neq q)$ is $\binom{\pi(N)}{2} \approx \frac{1}{2} \pi(N)^2$.

> The system possesses a **quadratic surplus** of "ammunition" relative to the linear number of "targets" (even numbers up to $2N$).

*Proof.* The first part is immediate. For the second, note that each unordered pair of distinct primes $\{p, q\}$ with $p, q \leq N$ gives a sum $p + q \leq 2N$. The number of such pairs is $\binom{\pi(N)}{2}$. By the Prime Number Theorem, $\pi(N) \sim N / \log N$, so $\binom{\pi(N)}{2} \sim \frac{1}{2} (N / \log N)^2$. $\square$

---

## 4. Structural Entropy and Anti-Symmetry

Redundancy is necessary but not sufficient for coverage. We must prove that the generators do not cluster to leave specific holes.

### 4.1 Structural Entropy

> **Definition 4.1 (Structural Entropy modulo $d$).** Let $A \subset [1, N]$ and let $d$ be a positive integer. For each residue $r$ (mod $d$), let $A_r = A \cap \{x \in [1, N] : x \equiv r \pmod{d}\}$. Define the *structural entropy* of $A$ modulo $d$ as:
> $$\mathcal{H}_d(A) = -\sum_{\substack{r=0 \\ \gcd(r,d)=1}}^{d-1} \frac{|A_r|}{|A|} \log_2\left(\frac{|A_r|}{|A|}\right)$$
> where we only sum over residues $r$ that are coprime to $d$. The base-2 logarithm is used, so entropy is measured in bits.

> **Definition 4.2 (Total Structural Entropy).** The *total structural entropy* of $A$ up to $N$ is defined as the average over moduli $d \leq \sqrt{N}$ (with $d$ having no large prime factors, e.g., $d$ squarefree):
> $$\mathcal{H}(A) = \frac{1}{D} \sum_{d \leq \sqrt{N}} \mathcal{H}_d(A)$$
> where $D$ is the number of such $d$.

> **Condition 4.1 (Generative Ergodicity / Gap-Filling Postulate).** The set of primes $A$, generated by the Gap-Filling process ($n=1$ Principle), tends towards **maximal structural entropy**. Specifically, for each modulus $d$ (squarefree and $\leq \sqrt{N}$), the primes are quasi-uniformly distributed among the residue classes coprime to $d$, meaning that for each such $r$,
> $$|A_r| \sim \frac{\pi(N)}{\phi(d)} \quad \text{as } N \to \infty$$
> where $\phi(d)$ is Euler's totient function. Consequently, the entropy modulo $d$ satisfies:
> $$\mathcal{H}_d(A) \approx \log_2 \phi(d)$$

This condition is supported by the Prime Number Theorem for arithmetic progressions and underlies the **"maximal dispersion"** property of primes.

### 4.2 The Anti-Symmetry Theorem

> **Definition 4.3 (Semigroup Void).** A *Semigroup Void* at $2K$ is a state where $2K \notin \mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{poly}}^{(2)}(A)$. This implies:
> $$A \cap (2K - A) = \emptyset$$

> **Theorem 4.1 (Low Entropy of Voids).** If a Semigroup Void exists at $2K$, then the set $A$ has abnormally low structural entropy. In particular, for any modulus $d$, the entropy $\mathcal{H}_d(A)$ is bounded above by $\log_2 \phi(d) - 1$ (for large $N$), which is significantly below the maximum $\log_2 \phi(d)$.

*Proof.* Assume $A \cap (2K - A) = \emptyset$. Consider a modulus $d$ and let $R_d$ be the set of residues modulo $d$ that are coprime to $d$. For each $r \in R_d$, define the symmetric residue $s = 2K - r \pmod{d}$.

The condition $A \cap (2K - A) = \emptyset$ implies that for any $x \in A$ with $x \equiv r \pmod{d}$, we cannot have any $y \in A$ with $y \equiv s \pmod{d}$. Therefore, **we cannot have both residues $r$ and $s$ occupied simultaneously**.

This implies that at most half of the possible residue classes in $R_d$ can be occupied by the set $A$.

In the best case for entropy (uniform distribution over the allowed classes), the probability mass is concentrated on $\phi(d)/2$ classes. The resulting entropy is:
$$\mathcal{H} \leq \log_2(\phi(d)/2) = \log_2 \phi(d) - 1$$

This represents a **loss of 1 bit of information per modulus**. This contradicts the Generative Ergodicity condition ($\mathcal{H} \approx \log_2 \phi(d)$). Therefore, a Semigroup Void forces the primes to have low structural entropy, which is incompatible with their generative nature. $\square$

---

## 5. Duality Dictionary and Program Roadmap

### 5.1 Purpose and Scope

This paper is part of a **two-perspective program** on sieve-generated arithmetic. We study Goldbach's conjecture simultaneously in:

| Framework | Perspective | Object of Study |
|:----------|:------------|:----------------|
| **Sieve-Theoretic (Dynamic)** | "sieve physics" | The prime indicator $D_S(n)$ generated by a local procedure |
| **Additive-Semigroup (Static)** | "additive geometry" | The set of primes $A$ as a generator set, sumset $A + A$ |

The key point is that a Goldbach counterexample defines the **same structural anomaly** in both languages, but each language exposes a different obstruction: **work/irreducibility** (dynamic) versus **entropy/anti-symmetry** (static).

### 5.2 Objects and Notation

Fix a sieve $S$ generating a binary predicate $D_S: \mathbb{N} \to \{0,1\}$, and define the prime set (generators) up to scale $N$ by:
$$A_N \coloneqq \{n \leq N : D_S(n) = 1\}$$

For an even target $2K$, define:
- The **sieve correlation functional**: $C_{2K}(S) \coloneqq \sum_{x=1}^{2K-1} D_S(x) D_S(2K - x)$
- The **additive sumset**: $A_N + A_N \coloneqq \{a + b : a, b \in A_N\}$

### 5.3 The Duality Dictionary

> **Lemma 5.1 (Goldbach-Failure Equivalences).** Let $N \geq 2K$ and $A_N = \{n \leq N : D_S(n) = 1\}$. Then:
> $$C_{2K}(S) = 0 \iff A_N \cap (2K - A_N) = \emptyset \iff 2K \notin (A_N + A_N)$$

*Proof.* By definition, $C_{2K}(S)$ counts solutions to $x + (2K - x) = 2K$ with both terms in $A_N$. Hence $C_{2K}(S) = 0$ iff there is no $a \in A_N$ with $2K - a \in A_N$, i.e., $A_N \cap (2K - A_N) = \emptyset$, which is equivalent to $2K \notin A_N + A_N$. $\square$

Beyond this definitional equivalence, each framework supplies a distinct obstruction mechanism against the same anomaly:

| Framework | Anomaly Name | Obstruction Mechanism |
|:----------|:-------------|:----------------------|
| **Sieve / Dynamic** | Resonant State | implies an oracle / speedup (work violation) |
| **Semigroup / Static** | Semigroup Void | forces anti-symmetry and low structural entropy |

### 5.4 Roadmap: Two Complementary Impossibility Arguments

We can view the overall argument as a **"two-detector" test** of the same forbidden state:

| Route | Detector | Mechanism |
|:------|:---------|:----------|
| **R1** | Dynamic / Work Detector | Assume a resonant state $C_{2K}(S) = 0$. Then for many indices $m = 2K - p$ (with $p$ prime), the compositeness of $m$ becomes available at $O(1)$ marginal cost, producing an algorithmic speedup incompatible with the conservation/irreducibility postulates of sieve-generated arithmetic. |
| **R2** | Static / Entropy Detector | Assume a semigroup void $2K \notin A_N + A_N$, equivalently $A_N \cap (2K - A_N) = \emptyset$. Then the residue-class support of $A_N$ modulo many small $d$ is forced into an anti-symmetric configuration, reducing its structural entropy by a constant amount per modulus, which conflicts with the quasi-uniform (high-entropy) distribution expected from the gap-filling generative principle. |

### 5.5 Interpretation

The duality is not merely rhetorical: it isolates two independent **"resources"** that a Goldbach counterexample would have to violate simultaneously:

| Resource | Violation |
|:---------|:----------|
| **Algorithmic** | would create free certificates of compositeness (work deficit) |
| **Statistical** | would enforce global anti-symmetry (entropy deficit) |

Thus, the sieve and semigroup perspectives constrain the same putative anomaly from **two complementary sides**.

---

## 6. Conclusion

We have moved beyond heuristic arguments of "density" to a structural proof based on **Entropy and Duality**.

1. **Surplus:** There are quadratically many pairs.
2. **Entropy:** Primes are constructed to be maximally disordered (Gap-Fillers).
3. **Conflict:** A missing even number requires primes to be highly ordered (Anti-Symmetric), reducing entropy by 1 bit.

Thus, the **"Semigroup Void"** is a forbidden state in a system generated by the $n = 1$ Principle. Even numbers are the inevitable byproduct of the high-entropy mixing of additive atoms.

> **Key Takeaway:** The Goldbach conjecture is not an isolated arithmetic fact but a structural necessity arising from the tension between linear extension (monogenic addition) and nonlinear mixing (polygenic addition), enforced by the maximal entropy requirement of the gap-filling generative process.

---

This article is central to **Module XXXIV: Goldbach as Structural Necessity** and connects to:

| Module | Connection |
|:-------|:-----------|
| **Module XXXVI: Goldbach as Entropic Necessity** | The structural entropy argument is developed further |
| **Module XLIV: Additive Physics** | The distinction between monogenic and polygenic addition is foundational |
| **Module XLVIII: Anti-Fractal Dynamics** | The Gap-Filler principle aligns with the anti-fractal nature of primes |
| **Module XLIX: The Goldbach Compensator** | The density compensation argument complements the entropy argument |

# Goldbach's Conjecture as a Structural Necessity in Sieve-Generated Arithmetic
## Entropy Production and Relative Incompressibility in the Binary Sieve

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate, January 2026  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXIV, XXXVI, XLIV, XLV, XLVI

---

## Abstract

> **Disclaimer:** This work presents a structural argument within the framework of Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN). It operates within a specific generative model of arithmetic ($\mathfrak{N}_{\mathrm{S}}$) governed by algorithmic cost and entropy constraints. It does not claim to be a proof of Goldbach's Conjecture in the classical sense of Peano Arithmetic or ZFC set theory.

We propose that Goldbach's Conjecture is a necessary consequence of the **Entropy Production Principle** inherent to the Binary Sieve. Viewing the sieve as a deterministic but entropy-rich generator, we define a Local Sieve-Observer constrained by sequential processing limits. We demonstrate that the sequence of prime numbers exhibits relative incompressibility with respect to simple linear transformations. A "Resonant State" (a counterexample to Goldbach for $2N$) would imply a global, linear correlation between primes in $[1,N]$ and composites in $[N,2N]$. Such a correlation constitutes an algorithmic shortcut ("free information") that violates the sieve's thermodynamic-like irreversibility. Thus, the conjecture holds in $\mathfrak{N}_{\mathrm{S}}$ not by chance, but because its failure would imply a forbidden reduction in the system's algorithmic entropy.

**Keywords:** Goldbach conjecture, binary sieve, algorithmic entropy, Kolmogorov complexity, incompressibility, resonant state

---

## 1. Introduction

In the Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN), we treat natural numbers not as static Platonic objects, but as the output of a dynamic generation process: **the Sieve**. The distribution of prime numbers is viewed as an emergent property of this generative mechanism.

Classical approaches to Goldbach's Conjecture often struggle with the "Parity Problem" or the difficult statistical properties of primes. Here, we adopt a different perspective rooted in **Algorithmic Information Theory (AIT)**. We posit that the generation of primes is a process that converts algorithmic work into structural entropy.

> **The central thesis** of this paper is that a failure of Goldbach's Conjecture (a "Resonant State") represents a **Structural Singularity**. It would require the set of primes to conspire to avoid a specific sum $2N$. We show that such a conspiracy constitutes a "hidden pattern" that allows for massive data compression via a global affine map $(p \to 2N - p)$. We argue that such a state is forbidden in a Sieve-Generated Universe because it violates the principle that the sieve monotonically increases the complexity of the number field relative to local observers.

---

## 2. Entropy Production in the Binary Sieve

To understand why prime numbers cannot "conspire" to avoid a sum $2N$, we must first formalize the generative process and the limits of observation within the model.

### 2.1 The Binary Sieve as a Generator

As described in Additive Sieves [2], the Binary Sieve constructs the set of prime numbers through an iterative application of periodic layers. Let $D_n$ be the binary sequence representing the status of numbers up to step $n$.

1. **Initialization:** Start with a sequence of potentially infinite zeros.
2. **Iteration:** Identify the first unmarked number $p$ (a new prime).
3. **Layering:** Apply a sieve layer $S(p)$ with period $p$, marking all multiples of $p$ as composite (0).
4. **Feedback:** The modified sequence $D_{\text{new}}$ determines the next prime, closing the loop.

This process is deterministic, yet it produces a sequence $X = \lim D_n$ that exhibits **high complexity**. The position of the next prime depends on the interference of all previous prime cycles.

### 2.2 The Sieve-Observer

We must define "complexity" not in absolute terms (which is uncomputable), but relative to the generator's capabilities.

> **Definition 2.1 (Local Sieve-Observer).** An observer $\mathcal{O}$ in the AFN model is defined by the following constraints:
> 1. **Locality:** At step $N$, $\mathcal{O}$ has access only to the prime indicator string $X_N$ (primes $\leq N$).
> 2. **Sequentiality:** To determine the status of a number $m > N$, $\mathcal{O}$ must perform "work" equivalent to checking divisibility by primes $p \leq \sqrt{m}$.
> 3. **No Oracle:** $\mathcal{O}$ does not have access to pre-computed global correlations or lookahead tables.

### 2.3 The Principle of Entropy Production

From the perspective of the Sieve-Observer, the sieve acts as an **entropy source**.

> **Generative Principle 2.1 (Entropy Production / Sieve Irreversibility).** The Binary Sieve is a process that monotonically increases the informational complexity of the number field. Specifically, there exists a constant $c > 0$ such that for any extension range $\Delta N$, and up to lower-order terms within the observer's admissible description class:
> $$K_{\mathcal{O}}(X_{N + \Delta N} \mid X_N) \geq c \cdot \Delta N \tag{1}$$
> Crucially, this implies that no description scheme available to $\mathcal{O}$ allows for sublinear amortized information gain. Information about the compositeness of a number $m$ is distinct and irreducible; it requires specific "witnesses" (divisors) generated by the process.

> **Remark 2.1 (Justification).** This principle is grounded in the nature of the Binary Sieve. Each new prime $p$ introduces a periodic layer that eliminates multiples of $p$. The interference pattern of these layers is complex and appears random. The sieve does not contain any mechanism to create global linear correlations (like $x \mapsto 2N - x$) that would allow for compression. Empirical evidence from computational studies and cryptographic applications supports the pseudorandomness of primes.

This principle asserts that the sieve does not generate "free" global correlations. There are no algorithmic shortcuts (simple linear maps) that allow $\mathcal{O}$ to predict the primality of a range $[N, 2N]$ solely from $X_N$ with zero marginal cost.

---

## 3. Relative Incompressibility and Resonant States

### 3.1 Resonant State as an Anomaly

We define the failure of Goldbach's conjecture strictly in terms of information flow.

> **Definition 3.1 (Resonant State).** A *Resonant State* exists at an even integer $2N$ if, for all primes $p$ such that $3 \leq p \leq N$, the number $2N - p$ is composite.

If such a state exists, it implies a rigid, deterministic coupling between the set of primes $\mathcal{P}_N = \mathcal{P} \cap [1, N]$ and the set of composites in the reflected interval. Specifically, it implies the mapping:
$$\forall p \in \mathcal{P}_N \Rightarrow (2N - p) \notin \mathcal{P}$$
This is a **global linear correlation**.

### 3.2 The Compression Argument

We now demonstrate that a Resonant State violates the Entropy Production Principle.

> **Theorem 3.1 (Information Collapse).** If a Resonant State exists at $2N$, then the relative Kolmogorov complexity of the prime sequence extension is collapsed, violating the generative constraints of the Binary Sieve.

*Proof.* Consider the task of the Sieve-Observer $\mathcal{O}$ who knows primes up to $N$ (string $X_N$) and wants to describe the configuration of numbers in $[N, 2N]$.

**Scenario A (Normal Sieve Physics):** To determine the status of numbers in $[N, 2N]$, $\mathcal{O}$ must run the sieve. The distribution of composites is determined by the complex interference of prime cycles. The pattern exhibits high structural complexity and constitutes an entropy-rich configuration. The description length is high because the specific locations of composites depend on arithmetic details of specific divisors.

**Scenario B (Resonant State):** Assume Goldbach fails for $2N$. The observer receives a short message: "Resonance at $2N$". With this short message and the existing knowledge of $X_N$, the observer can immediately mark a massive subset of $[N, 2N]$ as composite:
$$\text{For every } p \text{ where } X_N[p] = 1, \text{ set } X_{2N}[2N - p] = 0.$$

There are approximately $\pi(N)$ such primes. This simple linear map $T(p) = 2N - p$ instantly identifies $\pi(N)$ composite numbers without running the sieve layer checks for those numbers.

This constitutes an **Algorithmic Shortcut**. The information about the compositeness of these $\pi(N)$ numbers, which normally requires distinct divisors (witnesses), is now derived "for free" from the structure of the lower primes.

We can formalize this compression. Let $K_{\mathcal{O}}(X_{2N} \mid X_N)$ denote the conditional complexity of $X_{2N}$ given $X_N$ from the perspective of $\mathcal{O}$. In the normal case, we expect:
$$K_{\mathcal{O}}(X_{2N} \mid X_N) \sim \pi(N) \log N$$
because the observer essentially needs to encode the new primes in $[N, 2N]$, each requiring about $\log N$ bits to specify.

In the resonant case, however, the observer can use the rule $T(p) = 2N - p$ to mark $\pi(N)$ numbers as composite. The only additional information needed is the value $2N$ (which requires $O(\log N)$ bits) and the knowledge that the resonant condition holds (which is a constant, say 1 bit, if we assume the observer is given this fact). Thus:
$$K_{\mathcal{O}}(X_{2N} \mid X_N) \leq O(\log N) + \pi(N) \cdot O(1)$$

The $\pi(N) \cdot O(1)$ term accounts for the fact that we still need to determine the status of the remaining numbers not covered by the reflection, but note that the reflection already covers $\pi(N)$ numbers. For large $N$, $\pi(N) \sim N / \log N$, so the bound becomes $O(\log N) + O(N / \log N)$, which is much smaller than the expected $\pi(N) \log N \sim N$.

This is a contradiction to the Entropy Production Principle, which requires that $K_{\mathcal{O}}(X_{2N} \mid X_N) \geq c \cdot N$ for some constant $c > 0$. Therefore, a Resonant State cannot exist. $\square$

---

## 4. The Structure of the Impossible

Why is this "shortcut" forbidden?

In the AFN framework, the sieve builds structure **layer by layer**. A Resonant State requires that the "gaps" in the sieve (the primes) line up perfectly with the "non-gaps" (composites) under a reflection $2N - x$.

This requires the primes to **conspire**. They must arrange themselves in $[1, N]$ such that their reflection exactly avoids all primes in $[N, 2N]$. The sieve dynamics is inherently **modular and periodic** (based on layers $S(p)$), whereas the reflection $x \mapsto 2N - x$ is an affine global symmetry **not preserved** by the additive layering process.

Therefore, a Resonant State represents a **Foreign Structure**—a pattern that cannot be generated by the local iterative rules of the Binary Sieve. It creates a state of "Anti-Symmetry" with abnormally low structural entropy.

> **Remark 4.1 (Connection to the Riemann Hypothesis).** The Riemann Hypothesis implies that the primes are distributed as regularly as possible (the error term in the Prime Number Theorem is as small as possible). A Resonant State would require a massive irregularity: the primes in $[1, N]$ would have to be arranged so that none of their reflections are prime. This would contradict the notion of maximum regularity. While not a formal proof, this connection suggests that Goldbach's Conjecture and the Riemann Hypothesis are both manifestations of the same underlying principle of order in the distribution of primes.

---

## 5. Implications for Foundations

This result clarifies the relationship between the AFN framework and classical number theory.

> **Remark 5.1 (On the limits of classical formalism).** Classical arithmetic (e.g., Peano Arithmetic or ZFC) treats the prime predicate as a static relation existing in a completed infinity. The AFN framework treats primality as the output of a temporal, energetic process. The difference is not merely ontological luxury, but the ability to express constraints on information flow and irreversibility, which classical formalisms abstract away. In AFN, computational cost and entropy are physical laws of the number field, making Goldbach's Conjecture a stability condition rather than a combinatorial coincidence.

---

## 6. Conclusion

We have reformulated Goldbach's Conjecture not as a problem of arithmetic coincidence, but as a problem of **algorithmic information flow**.

1. **The Binary Sieve is an entropy generator**; it produces a sequence of primes that implies no description scheme allowing sublinear information gain.
2. **A Goldbach counterexample (Resonant State)** would establish a global affine correlation $(p \to 2N - p)$ that acts as a "compression algorithm" or an "oracle of compositeness."
3. **This shortcut violates** the Sieve-Observer's constraints and the Entropy Production Principle.

Thus, within the Additive Physics of Natural Numbers, the Goldbach Conjecture is a theorem describing the **stability of the sieve's entropy generation**.

---

# Sieves, Waves, and the Physics of Goldbach
## Structural Interference and the Additive Spectrum of Natural Numbers

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate, January 2026  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXVII, XLIV, XLVIII

---

## Abstract

The distribution of Goldbach pairs $G(N)$ is often described as a chaotic "comet." In this paper, we demonstrate that this chaos is an illusion caused by the superposition of deterministic waves generated by the Binary Sieve. We formalize the Sieve Wave Equation $\Psi_N$ and introduce the Additive Spectral Amplitude $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}$ to quantify the constructive interference of prime layers. We reveal a rigid topography of the number line: **Primorials** act as Crystalline Lattices (Resonant Peaks), while **Powers of Two** act as White Noise (Dampening Valleys). Crucially, we prove that the structural amplitude is strictly bounded below by 1. We argue that since the "waves" of prime density are superimposed on a strictly positive baseline, and the sieve lacks the mechanism to generate perfect anti-correlations, a zero-amplitude state is physically impossible. This offers a structural explanation for Goldbach's Conjecture: the universe of numbers does not admit the "perfect anti-crystal" required to break the conjecture.

**Keywords:** Goldbach conjecture, binary sieve, wave interference, spectral amplitude, primorials, powers of two

---

## 1. Introduction: From Chaos to Spectrum

When we plot the number of ways an even number $N$ can be written as a sum of two primes, $G(N)$, we see a scattering of points. Classical number theory treats this as a probabilistic phenomenon. Within the Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN), we assert that **there is no probability involved**. The "scatter" is a **diffraction pattern** resulting from the interference of periodic constraints.

We propose a shift in perspective:

1. **Primality is a Wave Property:** Every prime $p$ generates a periodic potential $W_p$.
2. **Goldbach Pairs are Standing Waves:** A pair exists where two wave troughs align.
3. **The Comet is a Spectrum:** The vertical bands in the plot correspond to discrete energy levels of structural interference.

> **Key Insight:** The apparent chaos of Goldbach pairs is not randomness but the result of deterministic wave interference. The spectrum is structured, not random.

---

## 2. The Physics of the Sieve

### 2.1 The Wave Equation of the Sieve

Unlike probabilistic models, the Binary Sieve is deterministic. We can define the "Prime Wave Function" for a prime $p$ as a periodic indicator function.

> **Definition 2.1 (Prime Wave Function).** For a prime $p$, the wave function $W_p: \mathbb{N} \to \{0, 1\}$ is defined as:
> $$W_p(n) = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{if } n \equiv 0 \pmod{p} \\ 1 & \text{otherwise} \end{cases} \tag{1}$$
> This function is 1 if $n$ is "allowed" by prime $p$ (i.e., not a multiple), and 0 otherwise.

The global state of the sieve for a target sum $N$ is the **superposition (product)** of these waves for all basis primes $p \leq \sqrt{N}$:

> **Definition 2.2 (Sieve Wave Function).** For a target even number $N$, the sieve wave function $\Psi_N$ is defined as:
> $$\Psi_N(n) = \prod_{p \leq \sqrt{N}} W_p(n) \cdot W_p(N - n) \tag{2}$$

The counting function for Goldbach pairs is then the summation of this wave function over the domain:

> **Definition 2.3 (Goldbach Counting Function).**
> $$G(N) \approx \sum_{n=3}^{N/2} \Psi_N(n) \tag{3}$$

Value $\Psi_N(n) = 1$ if and only if both $n$ and $N - n$ are prime candidates (i.e., not divisible by any small prime up to $\sqrt{N}$).

---

## 3. The Additive Spectrum

The intensity of the wave $\Psi_N$ depends on how the phases of $W_p(n)$ and $W_p(N - n)$ align. This alignment is quantified by the **Additive Spectral Amplitude**.

> **Definition 3.1 (Spectral Amplitude / "Goldbachness").** The constructive amplitude of the sieve at $N$ is given by:
> $$\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) = \prod_{\substack{p \mid N \\ p > 2}} \left( \frac{p-1}{p-2} \right) \tag{4}$$

This formula—identical to the singular series in the Hardy-Littlewood conjecture—is interpreted here **physically**: it represents the **signal amplification due to constructive interference**.

### 3.1 Topography of the Spectrum

The number line exhibits distinct structural zones based on this amplitude.

> **Observation 3.1 (Primorials as Crystalline Lattices).** At Primorials ($N_k = 2 \cdot 3 \cdot 5 \cdots p_k$), the sieve waves are perfectly synchronized ($N \equiv 0 \pmod{p}$ for all primes up to $p_k$). The phase shift is zero. The system behaves like a **perfect crystal**, maximizing the density of allowed states.

> **Observation 3.2 (Powers of Two as White Noise).** At Powers of Two ($N = 2^k$), the sieve waves have maximum relative phase disorder ($N \not\equiv 0 \pmod{p}$ for odd $p$). The system behaves like **white noise**. Yet, even in this disordered state, the signal is not destroyed—it merely lacks amplification:
> $$\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(2^k) = 1.0 \quad \text{(Ground State)}$$

**Example 3.1 (Comparing Amplitudes).** Consider the contrast between a Primorial and a Power of Two:

| $N$ | Type | $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N)$ | Actual Goldbach Pairs |
|:---:|:-----|:-------------------------------:|:---------------------:|
| 30 | $2\cdot3\cdot5$ (Primorial) | $\frac{2}{1} \cdot \frac{4}{3} \approx 2.67$ | (7,23), (11,19), (13,17) — 3 pairs |
| 32 | $2^5$ (Power of Two) | 1.0 | (3,29), (13,19) — 2 pairs |

Even though $32 > 30$, the structural resonance of 30 yields a higher count.

**Table 1: Analogies Between Physical Systems and the Goldbach Spectrum**

| Physical System | Peaks (High Order) | Valleys (Disorder) |
|:----------------|:-------------------|:-------------------|
| Crystallography | Bragg Peaks (Diffraction) | Diffuse Scattering |
| Quantum Mechanics | Resonant States | Ground State |
| Acoustics | Constructive Interference | Destructive Interference |
| **Goldbach Model** | **Primorials** ($\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}} \geq 1$) | **Powers of 2** ($\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}} = 1$) |

---

## 4. The Impossibility of Total Destructive Interference

The central question is: **Can the number of pairs $G(N)$ ever collapse to zero?**

> **Lemma 4.1 (Base Density is Structurally Positive).** The Prime Number Theorem implies that the "raw material" for pairs exists. The expected base density of pairs (the Cramér model baseline) is:
> $$G_{\text{base}}(N) \sim \frac{N}{\log^2 N}$$
> This baseline is structurally enforced by the sieve's entropy generation.

> **Theorem 4.1 (Non-Vanishing Amplitude).** For any even $N$, the spectral amplitude is strictly bounded below by 1:
> $$\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \geq 1$$

*Proof.* Each factor in the product is of the form $\frac{p-1}{p-2}$ for $p > 2$ dividing $N$. Since $p-1 > p-2$, each factor is $>1$. For primes not dividing $N$, the factor is 1 (implicitly). The product over an empty set (e.g., for powers of 2) is 1. Hence, the sieve never generates a dampening factor $< 1$. $\square$

> **Theorem 4.2 (Structural Lower Bound — Sketch).** There exists a constant $\delta > 0$ such that for sufficiently large even $N$:
> $$G(N) \geq \delta \cdot \mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \cdot \frac{N}{\log^2 N} \tag{5}$$

*Argument.* The count $G(N)$ is essentially the interaction of the Base Density (Signal) and the Sieve Structure (Modulation):
$$G(N) = \text{Signal} \times \text{Modulation} + \text{Noise}$$

1. **Signal:** The base density is strictly positive ($\propto N / \ln^2 N$).
2. **Modulation:** The structural modifier $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N)$ is strictly $\geq 1$ (Theorem 4.1).
3. **Noise:** For $G(N)$ to be zero, the "error terms" (fluctuations in prime distribution) would have to coherently align to cancel the main term perfectly.

> **Observation 4.1 (The Law of Large Numbers for Primes).** The distribution of primes in arithmetic progressions follows a "quasi-random" law. While local fluctuations exist (order $\sqrt{N}$), they behave like **white noise** relative to the global linear constraint of Goldbach. White noise cannot generate the perfect Anti-Correlation (a "conspiracy" of values) required to nullify the positive signal. Thus, **total destructive interference is physically impossible** in this system.

> **Remark 4.1 (Connection to Sieve Theory).** Using formal sieve methods (e.g., Selberg sieve), one can rigorously derive the upper bound involving $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N)$. The difficulty in classical theory lies in the lower bound. Our "physical" argument suggests that the lower bound is guaranteed by the **entropy of the sieve process**, which forbids the formation of the low-entropy "Anti-Crystal" needed to zero out the count.

---

## 5. Epistemological Remark

This derivation provides a **physical explanation** for why Goldbach's conjecture holds, based on the wave mechanics of the sieve. It differs from a formal proof in Peano Arithmetic (PA). In PA, one must prove that no "conspiracy" of numbers exists using logical entailment. In AFN, we show that **the generator (the Sieve) lacks the physical mechanism to create such a conspiracy**.

The "valleys" of the Goldbach spectrum are not voids; they are simply regions of **unamplified, white-noise density**. The signal never disappears because the baseline is always positive, and the sieve cannot generate perfect anti-correlation.

---

## 6. Conclusion

The Goldbach Comet is **not a random cloud**. It is a **spectrum**.

- **Primorials** are the resonant peaks of the number line.
- **Powers of Two** are the dissonant valleys.

Between these extremes, every even number vibrates with a specific "Goldbachness" determined by its prime factors. The Conjecture holds because the sieve's wave mechanics allows for amplification or baseline transmission, but provides **no mechanism for total signal loss**.

> **Key Takeaway:** The universe of numbers does not admit the "perfect anti-crystal" required to break Goldbach's Conjecture. The waves of the sieve always leave a positive trace.

---

## 7. Connection to Codex Rerum

# The Additive Physics Manifesto
## A New Foundation for Arithmetic: Sieves, Waves, and Structural Necessity

**Author:** Kajetan Młynarski  
**Source:** Preprint on ResearchGate, January 2026  
**Related Codex Modules:** XXXVIII, XLIV, XLVIII, LII

---

## Abstract

This paper proposes a paradigm shift in number theory, treating the set of natural numbers $\mathbb{N}$ not as an abstract axiomatic construct, but as a physically realizable system governed by generative constraints. In Part I, we analyze the distribution of Goldbach pairs as a Diffraction Spectrum generated by the deterministic waves of the Binary Sieve. We introduce the Additive Spectral Amplitude ($\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}$) to quantify constructive interference, revealing a rigid topography where Primorials act as resonant peaks and Powers of Two as dampening valleys. In Part II, we outline a research program: **The Physics of Mathematical Reality**. We argue that classical axiomatization acts as a "lossy compression" of physical reality, creating "Mathematical Hallucinations"—logical possibilities that are generatively impossible. We introduce the Spectral Order Parameter $\eta$ to classify number systems and reframe mathematical truth as a thermodynamic state governed by the Generative Exclusion Principle.

**Keywords:** additive physics, Goldbach spectrum, spectral amplitude, mathematical hallucinations, generative exclusion, phase transitions

---

## Part I: The Goldbach Spectrum

---

## 1. Introduction: From Chaos to Spectrum

When we plot the number of ways an even number $N$ can be written as a sum of two primes, $G(N)$, we see a scattering of points known as the "Goldbach Comet." Within the Additive Physics of Natural Numbers (AFN), we assert that **there is no probability involved**. The "scatter" is a **diffraction pattern** resulting from the interference of periodic constraints, structurally isomorphic to optical Speckle Patterns [3].

We propose a shift in perspective:

1. **Primality is a Wave Property:** Every prime $p$ generates a periodic potential $W_p$.
2. **Goldbach Pairs are Standing Waves:** A pair exists where two wave troughs align.
3. **The Comet is a Spectrum:** The vertical bands correspond to discrete energy levels of structural interference.

---

## 2. The Physics of the Sieve

### 2.1 The Wave Equation of the Sieve

The Binary Sieve is a deterministic generator. We define the "Prime Wave Function" for a prime $p$ as:

> **Definition 2.1 (Prime Wave Function).**
> $$W_p(n) = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{if } n \equiv 0 \pmod{p} \\ 1 & \text{otherwise} \end{cases} \tag{1}$$

The global sieve state for a target sum $N$ is the superposition (product) of these waves:

> **Definition 2.2 (Sieve Wave Function).**
> $$\Psi_N(n) = \prod_{p \leq \sqrt{N}} W_p(n) \cdot W_p(N - n) \tag{2}$$

The Goldbach counting function is the sum:

> **Definition 2.3 (Goldbach Counting Function).**
> $$G(N) \approx \sum_{n=3}^{N/2} \Psi_N(n) \tag{3}$$

---

## 3. The Additive Spectrum

The intensity of $\Psi_N$ is quantified by the **Additive Spectral Amplitude**:

> **Definition 3.1 (Spectral Amplitude).**
> $$\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) = \prod_{\substack{p \mid N \\ p > 2}} \left( \frac{p-1}{p-2} \right) \tag{4}$$

This formula represents the **signal amplification due to constructive interference**.

### 3.1 Topography of the Spectrum

The number line exhibits distinct structural zones:

| Type | Example | $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}$ | Physical Analogy |
|:-----|:--------|:-----------------------------:|:-----------------|
| **Primorials** | $30 = 2\cdot3\cdot5$ | $> 1$ (e.g., 2.67) | Resonant Peaks / Crystals |
| **Powers of Two** | $32 = 2^5$ | $= 1$ | Ground State / White Noise |

**Figure 1:** The Goldbach Spectrum: Resonant Peaks vs. Ground State Valleys.

---

## 4. The Impossibility of Total Destructive Interference

> **Theorem 4.1 (Non-Vanishing Amplitude).** For any even $N$, the spectral amplitude is strictly bounded below by 1:
> $$\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \geq 1$$

*Proof.* Each factor $\frac{p-1}{p-2} > 1$ for primes $p > 2$ dividing $N$. For primes not dividing $N$, the factor is 1 (implicitly). The product over an empty set (powers of two) is 1. $\square$

> **Conjecture 4.1 (Structural Lower Bound).** There exists a constant $\delta > 0$ such that for sufficiently large $N$:
> $$G(N) \geq \delta \cdot \mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \cdot \frac{N}{\log^2 N} \tag{5}$$

**Example 4.1 (Numerical Evidence).** For $N = 10^6$, $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \approx 3.24$ (typical). The expected count is $\approx 11{,}200$. Empirical data shows $G(10^6) = 5{,}402$. The order of magnitude respects the lower bound dictated by $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{spec}}(N) \geq 1$. The non-vanishing of the amplitude acts as a hard physical floor.

### 4.1 Argument for the Conjecture

For $G(N)$ to be zero, the "error terms" (white noise fluctuations) would have to coherently align to cancel the positive Base Density perfectly. In the AFN framework, the sieve acts as a "quasi-random" generator [5]. It **structurally lacks the mechanism** to create the perfect "Anti-Correlation" required for such cancellation.

---

## Part II: The Research Program

---

## 5. Beyond Goldbach: The Physics of Mathematical Reality

The solution to the Goldbach problem presented above validates a broader methodology. It suggests that the set of natural numbers $\mathbb{N}$ is a **specific, physically stable "Universe,"** rather than an arbitrary axiomatic construct. This opens a new research program: **The Physics of Mathematical Structures**.

---

## 6. Hypothesis of Unique Stability

Why does our universe use the specific sequence of primes $P = \{2, 3, 5, 7, \ldots\}$? We propose that "Real Natural Numbers" occupy a **unique critical point**.

> **Definition 6.1 (Spectral Order Parameter).** For a number system with generated amplitudes $\{A(N)\}$, we define the order parameter $\eta$ as the Fano factor of the spectrum:
> $$\eta = \frac{\mathrm{Var}(A)}{\mathbb{E}[A]} \tag{6}$$

> **Hypothesis 6.1 (The Edge of Chaos).** Based on $\eta$, we can classify arithmetic universes:

| Phase | $\eta$ | Characteristics | Goldbach Status |
|:------|:------:|:----------------|:----------------|
| **Frozen Phase** | $\eta \approx 0$ | Periodic systems (e.g., generated by a single prime). Trivial structure. | Likely fails |
| **Gas Phase** | $\eta \gg 1$ | Purely random systems (Cramér model). No resonance. | Likely fails |
| **Critical Phase** | $\eta \sim 1$ | Our $\mathbb{N}$. Balanced between crystalline order (Primorials) and white noise (Powers of 2). | **Goldbach holds** |

**Figure 2:** Phase diagram of number systems. Our $\mathbb{N}$ sits at the critical point.

---

## 7. The Cost of Abstraction: Mathematical Hallucinations

Why has Goldbach's Conjecture remained unproven for centuries? We propose that the difficulty is an **artifact of the toolset**. Classical mathematics (e.g., Peano Arithmetic) achieves minimal entropy (compact theorems) by performing a **lossy compression** of reality. It abstracts away the "physical" cost of generating numbers.

> **Definition 7.1 (Mathematical Hallucination).** A *Mathematical Hallucination* is a hypothetical state that is:
> - **Logically consistent** with the abstract axioms of a system (logical possibility)
> - **Generatively impossible** within the generative process that defines the system's objects

**Example 7.1 (Goldbach Counterexample as Hallucination).** The statement "$\exists N: G(N) = 0$" is:
- **Logically consistent** with Peano axioms (PA does not encode the sieve's work cost)
- **Generatively impossible** in AFN (violates Conservation of Algorithmic Work)

This discrepancy explains the centuries-long search: mathematics has been chasing a **phantom created by over-abstraction**.

---

## 8. The Thermodynamics of Mathematical Truth

The practice of mathematics itself is a **physical process**. The brain (or computer) takes physical inputs (discrete objects) and abstracts rules.

- **Axioms as Physical Laws:** $1 + 1 = 2$ is an empirical observation of rigid bodies. In a fluid universe $(1 + 1 = 1)$, mathematics would differ.
- **Proof as Work:** Generating a proof requires thermodynamic work (Landauer's Principle [7]) to reduce entropy.

> **Principle 8.1 (Generative Exclusion Principle).** A mathematical state is **impossible** if the generative mechanism lacks the information-theoretic capacity to produce it.

We postulate that the search for a Goldbach counterexample is analogous to the search for a **Perpetual Motion machine**: logically imaginable in a frictionless model, but **physically forbidden** by the conservation laws of the generator.

---

| **2** | Additive Spectroscopy for Twin Primes |
| **3** | Numerical study of "Alien Arithmetic" (Phase Transitions) |
| **4** | Formal isomorphism with Quasicrystals |
| **5** | Axiomatic foundation for AFN independent of Peano |

---

## 10. Conclusion

We are moving from a **descriptive mathematics** to a **generative physics**.

- **Primorials** are the "Diamonds" of the number world.
- **Powers of Two** are the "Background Radiation."
- **Goldbach's Conjecture** is the observation that this universe has **no "black holes"** — no regions where the signal of existence is completely extinguished.

> **Key Takeaway:** The natural numbers are not an arbitrary set but a physically stable configuration at the critical point between order and chaos. The Goldbach conjecture holds because the generative process lacks the mechanism to create voids.
